و(أل): في الروح للاستغراق، فهي دالة على العموم، والمراد جميع أرواح الثقلين ولو أرواح الشهداء براً وبحراً، وأرواح الملائكة حتى روح نفسه على أحد القولين ، وقيل : القابض لروحه هو الله عز وجل وأرواح البهائم والطيور وغيرهم، ولو بعوضة كما ذهب إليه أهل الحق، خلافاً للمعتزلة حيث ذهبوا إلى أنه لا يقبض أرواح غير الثقلين من الملائكة والطيور وغيرهم، وللمبتدعة حيث ذهبوا إلى أنه لا يقبض أرواح البهائم، بل يقبضها أعوانه، وقد أشار المصنّف للرد على الجميع بأل الدالة على العموم، ولمباشرة ملك الموت لذلك أسند إليه التوفي، كما في قوله تعالى : وَقُلْ يَتَوَفَّنَكُم مَّلَكُ الْمَوْتِ الَّذِى وُكِّلَ بِكُمْ [السجدة: 11]، وكَنسبته إلى أعوانه لمعالجتهم نزعها من العصب والعظم والعروق في قوله تعالى: تَوَفَّتْهُ رُسُلُنَا [الأنعام: 61]، وأما إسناد التوفي إليه تعالى في قوله تعالى : اللَّهُ يَتَوَفَّى الْأَنفُسَ حِينَ مَوْتِهَا [الزمر: 42]؛ فلأنه الخالق لذلك حقيقة الموجد له.
فائدة مجيء الموت والعبد على عمل صالح يسهل الموت، وكذلك السواك فيما ذكره جماعةٌ، ومما يُسهل الموت وجميع ما بعده من الأهوال ما ذكره السنوسي وغيره من صلاة ركعتين ليلة الجمعة بعد المغرب يقرأ بعد الفاتحة الزلزلة خمس عشرة، ورُوي أن سورتها تعدل نصف القرآن.
And 'al' in 'al-ruh' is for total inclusion (istighraq), so it indicates generality, and what is meant is all the souls of the two heavy groups (thaqalayn: humans and jinn) even the souls of martyrs on land and sea, and the souls of angels, even his own soul according to one of the two sayings. And it is said: the one who takes his soul is Allah, may He be exalted. And the souls of animals, birds, and others, even a mosquito, as Ahl al-Haqq went to, contrary to the Mu'tazila who went to that he does not take the souls of other than the thaqalayn from the angels, birds, etc., and contrary to the innovators (mubtadi'a) who went to that he does not take the souls of animals, rather his helpers take them. And the author indicated refutation of all by 'al' which indicates generality. And because the Angel of Death directly does that, the taking (tawaffi) is attributed to him, as in His saying: 'And say: the Angel of Death who is entrusted with you will take you' (Sajda 11), and like attribution to his helpers for their handling of its extraction from nerves, bones, and veins in His saying: 'Our messengers take him' (An'am 61). And as for attribution of tawaffi to Him, the Exalted, in His saying: 'Allah takes the souls at the time of their death' (Zumar 42); because He is the Creator of that, the true originator (al-mujid).
Benefit: The coming of death upon the servant while he is in a righteous deed facilitates death, and likewise the siwak, as a group mentioned. And among that which facilitates death and all the terrors after it is what Sanusi and others mentioned: two rak'ahs on Friday night after maghrib, reciting after al-Fatiha [surah] al-Zalzala fifteen times, and it is narrated that its surah is equivalent to half the Quran.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage clarifies two connected issues: the scope of the word 'al-ruh' (the soul) in the poem, and the correct attribution of death. First, the commentator states that the definite article 'al' in 'al-ruh' is for 'istighraq' (total inclusion), meaning it encompasses all souls: humans, jinn, angels, martyrs, and even animals. He then refutes two opposing views: the Mu'tazila who deny that the Angel of Death takes souls of other than humans and jinn, and the innovators (mubtadi'a) who deny that he takes animal souls, claiming his helpers do. The poem's use of 'al' refutes both. Second, the passage explains the different attributions of death (tawaffi) in the Quran. It is attributed to the Angel of Death because he directly executes the taking; to his helpers (angels) because they physically extract the soul; and to Allah because He is the true Creator and Originator of the act. This resolves apparent contradictions in Quranic verses. Finally, a 'benefit' (fa'ida) is added: performing righteous deeds, using a siwak, and a specific prayer on Friday night can ease the pangs of death and the terrors that follow.

Correction: The passage shows each attribution corresponds to a different level of causation: direct agent, physical extraction, and ultimate creation.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's attributions of death are compatible: Allah creates, the Angel of Death takes, and helpers extract the soul; plus, righteous deeds and a specific prayer can ease death.

The Killed Person Dies by His Appointed Term
Commentary on a poem line about the killed person's term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the position of Ahl al-Haqq regarding the appointed term (ajal) of a killed person: that it is fixed, one, and does not increase or decrease, and how to reconcile hadiths about deeds increasing lifespan.

Core Idea
The killed person dies exactly at his divinely appointed term; nothing changes it.

This lesson explains a key line from the poem stating that the killed person dies by his appointed term. The commentator clarifies the grammar and doctrinal significance, affirming that according to Ahl al-Haqq, the term of death is single and unchangeable. We'll also see how to understand narrations that mention increasing lifespan through good deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the poem line and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic poem line and its literal translation. Notice the key terms 'ajal' and 'umr'.
The poet uses 'umr' for meter, but the intended meaning is the end of life.
2
Understand the grammatical analysis
The commentator explains that 'dead' is a predicate preceding the subject. He also notes the need to supply an omitted genitive because 'umr' is used instead of 'ajal'.
If 'ajal' were used, no estimation would be needed.
3
Grasp the core doctrine
The passage affirms that ajal is one, fixed, and does not increase or decrease, citing Quran and hadith. It also begins to address the apparent contradiction from hadith about deeds increasing lifespan.
The full refutation is cut off, but the principle is clear: ajal is unchangeable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقتولُ مَيْتُ بأجلِهِ
ومَيِّتٌ بِعُمْرِهِ مَنْ يُقْتَلُ وغَيْرُ هَذَا بَاطِلٌ لا يُقْبَلُ
قوله : ( ومَيِّتُ بِعُمْرِهِ مَنْ يُقْتَلُ) (ميت) خبرٌ مقدَّم ، و (من يقتل) مبتدأ مؤخَرُ ؛ أي: كل ذي روح يفعل به ما يزهق روحه ميت بانقضاء عمره، ففي عبارة المصنف حذف مضاف، ولو عبر بالأجل لم يحتج لتقدير المضاف؛ لأن الأجل يطلق على آخر العمر، كما يطلق على مدة العمر بتمامها، لكن المصنف عبر بالعمر لأجل النظم، فاحتيج لتقدير المضاف . وما ذكره الناظم هو مذهب أهل الحق ، فالأجل عندهم واحد لا يقبل الزيادة والنقصان، قال تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا جَاءَ أَجَلُهُمْ لَا يَسْتَأْخِرُونَ سَاعَةً وَلَا يَسْتَقْدِمُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف : ٣٤]، وقد دلت الأحاديثُ على أن كل هالك يستوفي أجله من غير تقدم عليه ولا تأخر عنه، ولا تعارض هذه القواطع ما ورد بأن بعض الطاعات كصلة الرحم يزيد في العمر ؛ لأنه
The killed one is dead by his appointed term.
And dead by his lifespan is he who is killed, and other than this is false, not accepted.
His saying: 'And dead by his lifespan is he who is killed' – (dead) is a predicate introduced, and (who is killed) is a delayed subject; meaning: every soul that is acted upon in a way that causes its soul to depart is dead by the expiration of its lifespan. So in the expression of the author there is a deletion of a genitive (mudaf), and if he had expressed by 'ajal' (appointed term) there would be no need to estimate the genitive; because 'ajal' is used for the end of life, as it is used for the entire duration of life. But the author used 'lifespan' for the sake of the poem, so estimation of the genitive was needed. And what the versifier mentioned is the school of Ahl al-Haqq. For the appointed term (ajal) according to them is one, not accepting increase or decrease. Allah said: 'So when their term comes, they will not delay an hour nor advance' (A'raf 34). And the hadiths have indicated that every perishing person fulfills his term without being brought forward or delayed; and these definitive texts are not contradicted by what has come that certain acts of obedience like maintaining kinship ties increase lifespan, because...
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from the poem of Jawharat al-Tawhid. The line states: 'The killed one is dead by his appointed term' and 'dead by his lifespan is he who is killed; other than this is false, not accepted.' The commentator begins by analyzing the grammar of the second hemistich: 'dead' (ميت) is a predicate preceding the subject 'who is killed' (من يقتل). The meaning is that every living being whose soul is caused to depart dies at the expiration of its lifespan (umr). He notes that the poet used 'umr' instead of 'ajal' for poetic meter, which requires supplying an omitted genitive (i.e., 'by his lifespan' meaning 'by the end of his lifespan'). If 'ajal' had been used, no such estimation would be needed, because 'ajal' can mean either the end of life or the entire duration. The commentator then affirms that this is the position of Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth): the appointed term (ajal) is a single, fixed point that does not increase or decrease. He quotes the Quranic verse (A'raf 34) that when the term comes, no delay or advance is possible. He further notes that hadiths confirm that every dying person completes his exact term without any change. Finally, he addresses an apparent objection: that certain deeds like maintaining family ties are said to increase lifespan. These, he says, do not contradict the definitive texts, because... (the explanation is cut off in the source). The core doctrine is that ajal is unchangeable, and the killed person dies precisely at his predetermined time.

عمر
مقتول
أهل الحق
صلة الرحم

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The appointed term of death can be increased or decreased by human actions or circumstances.
Correction: The passage affirms that ajal is one and does not accept increase or decrease; what appears to be an increase is either metaphorical or refers to the perceived lifetime.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Ahl al-Haqq regarding the appointed term (ajal) of a killed person?
A) It is determined after the act of killing.
B) It is one and does not accept increase or decrease.
C) It can be shortened by the killer.
D) It is different from the term of one who dies naturally.

Key Takeaway
The killed person dies exactly at his predetermined term, which is fixed and unchangeable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Attribution of Death to Allah and the Angels
Commentary explains why death is attributed to Allah, the Angel of Death, and the angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the act of taking life (tawaffi) is attributed to Allah, the Angel of Death, and the assisting angels according to the Ash'ari principle of secondary causation.

Core Idea
Death is ultimately created by Allah but directly caused by the Angel of Death.

This passage from Tuhfat al-Murid clarifies a potential confusion in Quranic verses that attribute the taking of souls to different agents. It shows that the Angel of Death and his assistants are the immediate agents, while Allah is the true Creator. Understanding this hierarchy preserves both the apparent meaning of the verses and the theological principle that all actions originate from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three attributions
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice that the act of taking life is attributed to three different entities: the Angel of Death, his assistants, and Allah Himself.
The passage uses Quranic verses to support each attribution.
2
Understand the role of the Angel of Death
The passage states that because the Angel of Death directly handles the taking of life, the act is attributed to him in the Quran (Sajdah: 11).
3
Grasp why the ultimate attribution goes to Allah
The passage explains that attribution to Allah (Zumar: 42) is because He is the true Creator and Author of the act, while the angels are only agents.
This resolves the apparent contradiction between verses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات الدالة على العموم، ولمباشرة ملك الموت لذلك أسند إليه التوفي، كما في قوله تعالى : ﴿قُلْ يَتَوَفَّاكُمْ مَلَكُ الْمَوْتِ الَّذِي وُكِّلَ بِكُمْ﴾ [السجدة: 11]، كنسبته إلى أعوانه لمعالجتهم نزعها من العصب والعظم والعروق في قوله تعالى: ﴿تَوَفَّتْهُ رُسُلُنَا﴾ [الأنعام: 61]، وأما إسناد التوفي إليه تعالى في قوله تعالى: ﴿اللَّهُ يَتَوَفَّى الْأَنْفُسَ حِينَ مَوْتِهَا﴾ [الزمر: 42]؛ فلأنه الخالق لذلك حقيقة الموجد له.
The sam‘iyyat (matters known from revelation) indicate generality, and because the Angel of Death directly handles the taking of life, the act of causing death is attributed to him, as in His statement: 'Say: the Angel of Death who has been entrusted with you will take you in death' [Sajdah: 11]; and it is attributed to his assistants because they handle the extraction of the soul from nerves, bones, and veins, as in His statement: 'Our messengers cause him to die' [An‘am: 61]; as for the attribution of taking in death to Him, the Exalted, in His statement: 'Allah takes the souls at the time of their death' [Zumar: 42]; it is because He is the true Creator and Author of that.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation of how the single act of taking life (tawaffi) is attributed to different agents. The author begins by stating that the sam‘iyyat (revealed texts) indicate a general principle: because the Angel of Death directly performs the act of seizing the soul, the Quran attributes the tawaffi to him. This is seen in Surah Sajdah, where the Angel of Death is said to take the souls. However, the angels under his command are also involved in the process—they extract the soul from the body parts, hence the attribution to 'our messengers' in Surah An‘am. Finally, the tawaffi is also attributed to Allah Himself in Surah Zumar, because He is the true Creator (al-khāliq) and the real Author (al-mūjid) of the act. The point is that the same event has multiple aspects: direct causation by angels as the immediate agents, and ultimate creation by Allah. This preserves both the Quranic verses and the Ash‘ari principle that actions are created by Allah while attributions can be made to secondary agents.

Key Terms
سَمْعِيَّات
مَلَك الموت
تَوَفِّي
خَلْق
كَسْب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Attributing death to the Angel of Death negates Allah's role as the sole creator.
Correction: The passage affirms that Allah is the true Creator and Author, while the Angel of Death is the immediate agent. Attribution to the angel does not diminish Allah's ultimate causality.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the taking of death attributed to Allah in the verse 'Allah takes the souls' (Zumar: 42)?
A) Because the Angel of Death acts independently.
B) Because Allah is the true Creator and Author of the act.
C) Because the angels do not actually take life.
D) Because the verse refers to a different kind of death.

Key Takeaway
The act of death is attributed to the Angel of Death as the direct agent, to his assistants as immediate handlers, and to Allah as the ultimate Creator, all without contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you contemplate your own death, do you truly believe that Allah alone is its Creator, or do you let secondary causes – like illness or accidents – dominate your perspective? What one change can you make today to live more aware that every breath is a gift from the ultimate Creator?
?
The angels who will extract your soul are mere agents carrying out Allah's command. How does this realization affect the urgency of your preparation for that moment? Will you today make a concrete commitment to increase good deeds that will be your companions when the Angel of Death arrives?
?
Allah attributes the same event to Himself and to the angels without contradiction. Do you see the hands of others in your life as independent of Allah’s will? What would it mean for you to hold firm that every success and trial comes directly from Allah, and how would that transform your gratitude and patience right now?

Three Practices That Ease the Pangs of Death
A benefit listing good deeds that alleviate the difficulties of death and the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three specific practices that can ease the difficulties of death and the grave, and the importance of being engaged in a righteous deed at the moment of death.

Core Idea
Righteous deeds, siwak, and a special Friday prayer ease death's hardship.

This lesson presents a reported benefit (fā’idah) from the Islamic tradition that identifies three actions which can alleviate the terrors of death and the grave. The passage cites the authority of Imam al-Sanusi and others for the most detailed practice, a specific prayer on Friday night. As you read, note how these practices combine righteous action, physical purification, and devotional worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: it begins with a general statement, then adds two more specific practices.
The Arabic uses 'فائدة' to mark this as a beneficial teaching.
2
Identify the three practices
Find each practice mentioned. List them: (1) being engaged in a righteous deed at death, (2) using the siwak, (3) praying two rak'ahs on Friday night after Maghrib reciting al-Zalzalah fifteen times.
The third practice is the most detailed, attributed to al-Sanusi.
3
Reflect on the nature of these benefits
Consider that these are recommended practices, not obligatory. They are means that may ease death, but ultimate ease depends on Allah's will. The passage does not provide proof but cites transmitted reports.
Avoid misunderstanding them as guarantees.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة مجيء الموت والعبد على عمل صالح يُسهل الموت، وكذلك السواك فيما ذكره جماعةٌ، ومما يُسهل الموت وجميع ما بعده من الأهوال ما ذكره السنوسي وغيره من صلاة ركعتين ليلة الجمعة بعد المغرب يقرأ بعد الفاتحة الزلزلة خمس عشرة مرة، ورُوي أن سورتها تعدل نصف القرآن.
A benefit: the coming of death while the servant is engaged in a righteous deed eases death, and likewise the siwak (tooth-stick) as mentioned by a group; and among what eases death and all the terrors after it is what al-Sanusi and others mentioned, namely two rak‘ahs on Friday night after Maghrib in which one recites after al-Fatihah the surah al-Zalzalah fifteen times, and it is narrated that this surah equals half of the Quran.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a reported benefit (fā’idah) dealing with practices that make the experience of death easier. The author presents three things: first, being engaged in a righteous deed at the moment of death makes death easy. Second, using the siwak (tooth-stick) is mentioned by a group of scholars as beneficial. Third, the most detailed point: Imam al-Sanusi and others mention that performing two rak‘ahs after Maghrib on Friday night, reciting Surat al-Zalzalah fifteen times after al-Fatihah, eases death and all the subsequent terrors. The author adds that this surah is reported to be equal to half the Quran. This benefit is presented as practical guidance within the discussion of death, relying on transmitted reports and the authority of earlier scholars. The passage does not prove these claims from primary sources but cites them as beneficial knowledge.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These practices guarantee an easy death regardless of Allah's will.
Correction: These are recommended means, not guarantees; ease ultimately depends on Allah's decree and the individual's faith.

Key Takeaway
Three practices—righteous deed at death, siwak, and a specific Friday prayer—are transmitted as means to ease death and its terrors.

?

The Fixed Term: One, Not Increased or Decreased
Affirmation of the fixed term with grammatical and Quranic basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core doctrine of Ahl al-Sunnah that every person's term (ajal) is single and unchangeable, based on the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
The term (ajal) of every soul is fixed; it cannot be advanced or delayed.

This passage from the Jawharat al-Tawhid commentary establishes the fundamental belief about the appointed term of death. The author affirms that every killed person dies precisely when his term expires, and no act can alter that moment. Before reading the commentary, note how the poet expresses this doctrine concisely.

Guided Path
1
Read the poetic line and grammatical explanation
Read the first part of the passage where the poet states 'The killed person dies by his term.' The commentator explains the grammar: 'dies' is a predicate, 'one who is killed' is the subject.
Note the author used 'lifespan' (umr) instead of 'term' (ajal) for rhyme.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
The passage cites Quran 7:34: 'When their term comes, they shall not delay it by an hour nor precede it.' This is the primary evidence that the term is fixed.
3
Understand the doctrinal conclusion
The commentator states that according to Ahl al-Haqq, the term is one and does not accept increase or decrease. This is the fundamental position.
This directly answers the question: can a person's lifespan change? No.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقتول ميت بأجله
وميت بعمره من يقتل وغير هذا باطل لا يقبل
قوله: (وميت بعمره من يقتل) (ميت) خبر مقدم، و(من يقتل) مبتدأ مؤخر؛ أي: كل ذي روح يفعل به ما يزهق روحه ميت بانقضاء عمره، ففي عبارة المصنف حذف مضاف، ولو عبر بالأجل لم يحتج لتقدير المضاف؛ لأن الأجل يطلق على آخر العمر، كما يطلق على مدة العمر بتمامها، لكن المصنف عبر بالعمر لأجل النظم، فاحتيج لتقدير المضاف. وما ذكره الناظم هو مذهب أهل الحق، فالأجل عندهم واحد لا يقبل الزيادة والنقصان، قال تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا جَاءَ أَجَلُهُمْ لا يَسْتَأْخِرُونَ سَاعَةً وَلا يَسْتَقْدِمُونَ﴾ [الأعراف: 34]، وقد دلت الأحاديث على أن كل هالك يستوفي أجله من غير تقدم عليه ولا تأخر عنه، ولا يعارض هذه القواطع ما ورد بأن بعض الطاعات كصلة الرحم يزيد في العمر؛ لأنه خير آحاد، أو أن الزيادة فيه بحسب الخير والبركة، أو بالنسبة لما ثبت في صحف الملائكة، فقد يثبت الشيء فيها مطلقاً، وهو في علم الله تعالى مقيد، كأن يكون في صحف الملائكة: إن عمر زيد خمسون مثلاً مطلقاً، وهو في علم الله تعالى مقيد بأن لا يفعل كذا من الطاعات، وإن فعلها فله ستون، فإن سبق في علمه تعالى أنه يفعلها فلا يتخلف عن فعلها وكان عمره ستين فالزيادة بحسب الظاهر على ما في صحف الملائكة، وإلا فلا بد من تحقق ما في علمه تعالى كما يشير له قوله تعالى: ﴿يَمْحُوا اللَّهُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيُثْبِتُ وَعِنْدَهُ أُمُّ الْكِتَابِ﴾ [الرعد: 39]؛ أي: أصل اللوح المحفوظ؛ وهو علمه تعالى الذي لا محو فيه ولا إثبات، وأما اللوح المحفوظ فالحق قبول ما فيه للمحو والإثبات كصحف الملائكة، وبعضهم فسر أم الكتاب باللوح المحفوظ؛ لأنه ما من كائن إلا وهو مكتوب فيه والراجح الأول، وبالجملة فمختار أهل السنة أن كل مقتول ميت بانقضاء عمره، وحضور أجله في الوقت الذي علم الله حصول موته فيه أزلاً، بخلقه تعالى من غير مدخلية للقاتل فيه، وإنما وجب عليه القصاص نظراً للكسب فقط؛ وعند أهل السنة أنه لو لم يقتل لجاز أن يموت في ذلك الوقت وألا يموت فيه؛ لأنه لا اطلاع لنا على ما في علم الله، فيحتمل أنه لو لم يقتل أن يموت في ذلك الوقت، إن لم يكن عمره في علم الله أكثر من ذلك، ويحتمل ألا يموت فيه إن كان عمره في علم الله أكثر.
The killed person dies by his term. And one who is killed dies by his lifespan; other than this is false and unacceptable. His statement: 'And one who is killed dies by his lifespan': (dies) is a predicate placed before, and (one who is killed) is a subject placed after; that is, every living being upon which something is done that extinguishes its soul is dead by the expiration of its lifespan. Thus in the author's expression there is an omitted genitive; if he had expressed it as 'term' (ajal) he would not have needed to supply the genitive because ajal is used for the end of life as well as for the entire duration. But the author used 'lifespan' (umr) for the sake of the rhyme, so the genitive had to be supplied. What the author stated is the doctrine of the people of truth (ahl al-haqq): for them the term (ajal) is one, not subject to increase or decrease. Allah says: 'When their term comes, they shall not delay it by an hour nor precede it' [A‘raf: 34]. Hadiths indicate that everyone who perishes fulfills his term without preceding or delaying it. These decisive proofs are not contradicted by what is reported that some acts of obedience like maintaining family ties increase lifespan, because this is a hadith of ahad (single-chain), or the increase is in terms of goodness and blessing, or relative to what is recorded in the books of the angels. For a thing may be recorded there absolutely, while in Allah's knowledge it is conditional: for example, in the angels' books: 'The lifespan of Zayd is fifty years' absolutely, but in Allah's knowledge it is conditional upon his not performing certain acts of obedience; if he does them, then he gets sixty. If it was preordained in Allah's knowledge that he will perform them, then he does not fail to act and his lifespan is sixty, so the increase is apparent relative to the angels' books. Otherwise, what is in Allah's knowledge must come to pass, as indicated by His statement: 'Allah erases what He wills and establishes, and with Him is the Mother of the Book' [Ra‘d: 39]; that is, the source of the Preserved Tablet (al-lawh al-mahfuz)—and it is His knowledge which is subject to no erasure or establishment. As for the Preserved Tablet, it is possible for what is in it to accept erasure and establishment like the angels' books. Some have interpreted 'Mother of the Book' as the Preserved Tablet because every being is written in it, but the preferred view is the first. In summary, the chosen doctrine of Ahl al-Sunnah is that every killed person dies by the expiration of his lifespan and the arrival of his term at the time Allah knew from eternity his death would occur, by His creation without any involvement of the killer in it; the killer only incurs retribution from the perspective of the act of acquisition (kasb). According to Ahl al-Sunnah, if he had not been killed, it is possible that he would have died at that same time and possible that he would not have died then, because we have no knowledge of what is in Allah's knowledge. Thus it is possible that if he had not been killed he would have died at that time if his lifespan in Allah's knowledge was no longer than that, and possible that he would not have died then if his lifespan in Allah's knowledge was longer.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive doctrinal discussion of the fixed term (ajal) of the killed person. It begins with the poetic line: 'The killed person dies by his term. And one who is killed dies by his lifespan; other than this is false and unacceptable.' The commentator then explains the line grammatically: 'dies' is a predicate placed before the subject 'one who is killed'. The meaning: any living entity that is acted upon to extinguish its soul dies when its lifespan expires. The author uses 'lifespan' (umr) instead of 'term' (ajal) for the sake of the poem's meter, but ajal would have been more precise. The core doctrine of Ahl al-Haqq is that the term (ajal) is single and cannot increase or decrease. The commentator supports this with the Quranic verse from Surah A‘raf and with hadiths stating that everyone fulfills their term exactly. Then an objection is raised: hadiths like 'maintaining family ties increases lifespan' seem to contradict this. The commentator gives three reconciliations: (1) the hadith is ahad (single-chain) and thus not decisive; (2) the increase is in goodness and blessing, not actual years; (3) the increase is relative to the angels' books (lower records), while in Allah's eternal knowledge the term is conditional. A detailed example: the angels' books record Zayd's lifespan as fifty unconditionally, but in Allah's knowledge it is conditional on his not performing certain acts of obedience; if he does them, it is sixty. If Allah knows eternally that he will perform them, the extra ten years are realized and the increase is only apparent in the lower records. This reconciles with the verse on erasure and establishment in Surah Ra‘d. The commentator explains that 'Mother of the Book' (umm al-kitab) is Allah's immutable knowledge, distinct from the Preserved Tablet which allows changes. The final summary states the position of Ahl al-Sunnah: every killed person dies exactly when Allah knew from eternity, with no real input from the killer except as an acquired act (kasb) that justifies retribution. Moreover, if the person had not been killed, it is possible that he would have died at that same time or later, depending on the hidden divine decree—thus preserving both divine foreknowledge and human responsibility.

عمر
المقتول
ميت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the view of Ahl al-Haqq regarding the term (ajal)?
A) It can increase through good deeds.
B) It is one and does not accept increase or decrease.
C) It is conditional and changes.
D) It applies only to believers.

Key Takeaway
The appointed term of death is single and unchangeable, as stated in the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your death is appointed by Allah and cannot be delayed or advanced by any action? How does this belief affect your fear of death and your reliance on Allah?
?
If you knew that your term is fixed, would you live differently? What would you change today to align your actions with the reality that you cannot control the moment of your death?
?
When you plan your life, do you act as if you can postpone death by precautions? How can you internalize that your term is one, not subject to increase or decrease, and let that shape your trust in Allah?

Reconciling Apparent Contradictions: Divine Knowledge and Lower Records
Reconciliation of hadiths and explanation of divine records

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Sunnah reconcile hadiths that seem to show lifespan increase (like through family ties) with the fixed term, and the distinction between Allah's eternal knowledge and the lower records.

Core Idea
Apparent increases in lifespan are relative to the angels' books, not the eternal divine decree.

After affirming the fixed term, the commentator addresses a common objection: how can we reconcile hadiths that say good deeds increase lifespan? This lesson presents the three main reconciliations and explains the subtle theology of divine knowledge and recorded tablets. The key is understanding that changes occur only in lower records, while Allah's knowledge is immutable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection from hadith
The passage mentions that hadiths like 'maintaining family ties increases lifespan' appear to contradict the fixed term. Recognize this as the challenge.
This is a common source of confusion.
2
Study the three reconciliations
The commentator offers three ways to harmonize: 1) the hadith is ahad (single-chain) and not decisive; 2) the increase is in goodness and blessing, not actual years; 3) the increase is relative to what is recorded in the angels' books.
The third reconciliation is the most detailed and important.
3
Work through the example of Zayd
The passage gives an example: Zayd's lifespan in the angels' books is fifty years unconditionally, but in Allah's knowledge it is conditional; if he performs good deeds, it becomes sixty. This illustrates how changes can be apparent in lower records.
This example clarifies the third reconciliation.
4
Understand the distinction between divine records
The commentator distinguishes between Umm al-Kitab (Allah's immutable knowledge) and the Preserved Tablet & angels' books (which allow erasure and establishment). This is the theological basis for the apparent changes.
The verse from Surah Ra'd supports this distinction.
5
Review the final position of Ahl al-Sunnah
The passage concludes that every killed person dies exactly at his term; the killer only acquires the act (kasb) for retribution. If not killed, the person might have died at the same time or later depending on Allah's hidden knowledge.
This preserves both divine foreknowledge and human responsibility.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that the hadith about lifespan increase literally contradicts the fixed term and therefore the term is not truly fixed.
Correction: The passage explains that the increase is relative to the angels' books, not the eternal decree, and does not contradict the fixed term. The term in Allah's knowledge remains single and unchangeable.

According to the passage, what is the status of the hadith that says maintaining family ties increases lifespan?

C) It contradicts the Quran and is therefore rejected.

Dispute Over the Soul's Annihilation at the First Trumpet Blast
Commentator presents two opinions on whether the soul perishes at the first trumpet blast and lists exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly opinions regarding the soul's annihilation at the first trumpet blast and the exceptions to the general rule of death at that blast.

Core Idea
Al-Subki held the soul survives the first blast; others disagree.

In this lesson, we examine a specific eschatological dispute: Does the soul perish at the first trumpet blast? The commentator presents two views and then clarifies the consensus before the blast and the exceptions. This discussion is part of the samiyyat section of theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the poem and explanation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that the poem sets up the dispute, and the commentary clarifies the terms.
The term 'nafs' here means 'ruh' (spirit).
2
Identify the two opposing opinions
Find the two groups: one holds annihilation based on Quran 55:26, the other holds non-annihilation.
3
Understand the consensus before the first blast
Note that before the first blast, Muslims agree the soul survives after death, experiencing reward or punishment.
4
Learn the exceptions
List the exceptions: the four chief angels, the houris, and Moses. Understand why Moses is excluded.
Moses was struck in the world once, so he is recompensed.
5
Reflect on al-Subki's position
Consider why al-Subki favored survival and how this passage fits into broader eschatology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخلاف في فناءِ الرُّوحِ] ٩٠ - وَفِي فَنَا النَّفْسِ لَدَى النَّفْخِ اخْتُلِفْ واسْتَظْهِرَ السُّبْكِي بَقَاهَا اللَّذْ عُرِفْ قوله : (وَفِي فَنَا النَّفْسِ لَدَى النَّفْخِ (اخْتُلِف :أي: وفي ذهاب صورة النفس التي هي الروح عند نفخ إسرافيل في الصور النفخة الأولى اختلف العلماء : فذهبت طائفة إلى الحكم بفنائها عند ذلك؛ لظاهر قوله تعالى : وكُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانِ [الرحمن : ٢٦] . وذهبت طائفةٌ أُخرى إلى الحكم بعدم فنائها عند ذلك، وأما قبل نفخ إسرافيل في الصور النفخة الأولى فلا خلاف بين المسلمين في بقائها، ولو بعد فناء الجسم، وتكون منعمةٌ إن كانت من أهل الخير، ومُعذبةٌ إن كانت من أهل الشر، وتُسمَّى النفخة الأولى نفخة الفناء ولا يبقى عندها حيّ إلا مات إن لم يكن مات قبل ذلك ؛ وإلا غشي عليه إن كان مات قبل ذلك كالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام، إلا من شاء الله كالملائكة الأربعة الرؤساء والحور العين وموسى عليه الصلاة والسلام؛ لأنه صُعِقَ في الدنيا مرةً فجُوزي بها، فجميع الأنبياء بعد الموت تعود إليهم أرواحهم، ثم يُغشى عند النفخة الأولى إلا موسى لما حصل له في الدنيا (٢) ، ثم ينفخ إسرافيل في
[Section on the dispute concerning the annihilation of the soul] 90 - And concerning the annihilation of the self (nafs) at the trumpet, there is dispute; and al-Subki held its survival to be the stronger view, which is known. His saying: 'And concerning the annihilation of the self at the trumpet, there is dispute' means: regarding the loss of the form of the self, which is the spirit (ruh), at the time of Israfil's blowing into the trumpet, the first blast, the scholars differed. A group held the ruling of its annihilation at that time, due to the apparent meaning of His saying: 'Everyone upon it will perish' (Quran 55:26). Another group held the ruling of its non-annihilation at that time. As for before Israfil's blowing of the first blast, there is no dispute among Muslims about its survival, even after the annihilation of the body; it is either blessed if it was among the people of good, or punished if it was among the people of evil. The first blast is called the blast of annihilation; no living being remains at it except it dies if it had not died before that; otherwise it is overwhelmed if it had died before that, like the prophets (peace be upon them), except whom God wills, such as the four chief angels, the houris, and Moses (peace be upon him) because he was struck in the world once and was recompensed for it. All prophets after death have their spirits returned to them, then they are overwhelmed at the first blast except Moses because of what happened to him in the world, then Israfil blows...
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition of a dispute regarding the fate of the soul at the first trumpet blast. It begins by citing the poem from Jawharat al-Tawhid, which states that there is a dispute about the annihilation of the self (nafs) at the trumpet, and that al-Subki preferred the view of its survival. The commentator explains: 'self' here means the spirit (ruh). The dispute arises among scholars: one group holds that the soul perishes at the first blast, based on Quran 55:26. Another group holds that it does not perish. Before the first blast, there is consensus that the soul survives even after the body's death, experiencing reward or punishment. The first blast is called the blast of annihilation; every living being dies at it, except that those who died previously are overwhelmed (become unconscious) rather than die again. This includes the prophets, except for four archangels, the houris, and Moses, because Moses was already struck in the world. The explanation then notes that all prophets have their souls returned after death, then are overwhelmed at the first blast, except Moses. The passage ends mid-sentence with the second blast following.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul is annihilated along with the body at the first trumpet blast.
Correction: While some scholars hold that view, the stronger view, as favored by al-Subki, is that the soul survives. Moreover, before the blast, there is consensus on the soul's continued existence after bodily death.

Checkpoint

The survival of the soul at the first trumpet blast is supported by al-Subki, and the passage clarifies exceptions where certain beings are not affected.

?

Dispute over the Soul's Annihilation at the First Trumpet Blast
The author details the dispute over whether the soul perishes at the first trumpet blast and presents Subki's preferred view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly disagreement about whether the soul perishes at the first trumpet blast, and why al-Subki favored its survival based on istishab.

Core Idea
The soul’s survival after the first blast is defended by consensus and the principle of continuity.

The fate of the soul at the first trumpet blast is a matter of debate. Some scholars infer annihilation from the Qur'anic verse 'Everyone upon it will perish,' while others argue for survival. This lesson presents both views and highlights al-Subki's preferred position, grounded in the presumption of continuity (istishab).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once for flow, then the translation. Notice the poem line and the commentary structure.
The passage is a commentary on a poem from 'Jawharat al-Tawhid'.
2
Identify the two opposing views
One group says the soul perishes at the first blast, citing Qur'an 55:26. The other says it does not perish.
The disagreement is only about the first blast; before that, consensus on survival.
3
Understand the exceptions and the second blast
Note that prophets and others faint at the first blast, and the second blast is for resurrection. The soul returns to the body through holes in the Trumpet.
The exception of Moses is due to his prior unconsciousness in the world.
4
Analyze al-Subki's argument for survival
Al-Subki uses consensus on survival after death for grave questioning and the principle of istishab (what remains continues unless proven otherwise). Thus the soul is excepted from annihilation.
His view is considered the chosen one among Ahl al-Haqq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخلاف في فناءِ الرُّوحِ]
٩٠ - وَفِي فَنَا النَّفْسِ لَدَى النَّفْحَ اخْتُلِفْ واسْتَظْهِرَ السُّبْكِي بَقَاهَا اللَّذْ عُرِفْ
قوله : (وَفِي فَنَا النَّفْسِ لَدَى النَّفْخِ (اخْتُلِف :أي: وفي ذهاب صورة النفس التي هي الروح عند نفخ إسرافيل في الصور النفخة الأولى اختلف العلماء : فذهبت طائفة إلى الحكم بفنائها عند ذلك؛ لظاهر قوله تعالى : ﴿كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانِ﴾ [الرحمن : ٢٦] . وذهبت طائفةٌ أُخرى إلى الحكم بعدم فنائها عند ذلك، وأما قبل نفخ إسرافيل في الصور النفخة الأولى فلا خلاف بين المسلمين في بقائها، ولو بعد فناء الجسم، وتكون منعمةٌ إن كانت من أهل الخير، ومُعذبةٌ إن كانت من أهل الشر، وتُسمَّى النفخة الأولى نفخة الفناء ولا يبقى عندها حيّ إلا مات إن لم يكن مات قبل ذلك ; وإلا غشي عليه إن كان مات قبل ذلك كالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام، إلا من شاء الله كالملائكة الأربعة الرؤساء والحور العين وموسى عليه الصلاة والسلام؛ لأنه صُعِقَ في الدنيا مرةً فجُوزي بها، فجميع الأنبياء بعد الموت تعود إليهم أرواحهم، ثم يُغشى عند النفخة الأولى إلا موسى لما حصل له في الدنيا (٢) ، ثم ينفخ إسرافيل في الصور النفخة الثانية، وتُسمَّى نفخة البعث، فيجمع الله الأرواح في الصور عند النفخة الثانية، وفيه نَقْبٌ ،بعددها، فتخرج منه الأرواح إلى أجسادها، فلا تُخطئ روح جسدها، وبين النفختين أربعون عاماً على ما في بعض الطرق (۱) . قوله : (وَاسْتَظْهِرَ السُّبْكِي بَقَاهَا اللَّدْ عُرِف بتخفيف الياء وتسهيل ألف بقاها، وتسكين الذال لغة في (الذي) (٢) اختار الإمام تقي الدين السبكي في تفسيره المسمَّى بـ «الدر النظيم من هذا الاختلافِ القول ببقائها الذي عهد سابقاً؛ لأنهم اتفقوا على بقائها بعد الموت لسؤالها في القبر وجوابها وتنعيمها أو تعذيبها فيه، والأصل في كل باق استمراره حتى يظهر ما يصرف عنه، فالدليل على بقائها الاستصحاب، فتكون من المستثنى بقوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا مَن شَاءَ اللهُ﴾ [النَّمل : ۸۷]، وما قاله السبكي هو المختار عند أهل الحق، وإنما خصه المصنف بالذكر لتبحُرِه في الفنون حتى أحاط بالمعقول والمنقول.
[The dispute over the annihilation of the soul] 90 - And concerning the annihilation of the soul at the blast, there is disagreement, and al-Subki preferred its survival, as is known. His saying: 'And concerning the annihilation of the soul at the blast, there is disagreement' means: Regarding the passing away of the form of the soul (nafs), which is the spirit (ruh), at the blowing of Israfil in the Trumpet—the first blast—the scholars differed. A group held that it perishes at that time, due to the apparent meaning of His statement: 'Everyone upon it will perish' [al-Rahman 55:26]. Another group held that it does not perish at that time. As for before Israfil's blowing of the first blast, there is no disagreement among Muslims that it remains, even after the body's annihilation; it is rewarded if it was among the people of good and punished if it was among the people of evil. The first blast is called the blast of annihilation; no living being remains at it except that it dies if it had not died before, otherwise it is overcome with unconsciousness if it had died before, like the prophets (peace and blessings upon them), except those whom God wills, such as the four archangels, the houris, and Moses (peace be upon him) because he was struck unconscious in the world once and was recompensed with it. So all the prophets, after death, their souls return to them, then they are overcome with unconsciousness at the first blast, except Moses due to what happened to him in the world. Then Israfil blows the second blast, called the blast of resurrection. God gathers the souls in the Trumpet at the second blast, and it has holes equal to their number; the souls come out from it to their bodies, and no soul misses its body, and between the two blasts is forty years according to some narrations. His saying: 'and al-Subki preferred its survival as is known'—with lightening of the ya and simplification of the alif of 'baqaha', and stilling of the dhal as a dialect in 'alladhi'—Imam Taqi al-Din al-Subki chose in his commentary called 'al-Durr al-Nazim' from this disagreement the opinion of its survival as previously known, because they agreed on its survival after death for its questioning in the grave, its answering, and its being rewarded or punished therein. The principle regarding everything that remains is its continuity until something appears that diverts it; so the evidence for its survival is istishab (presumption of continuity). Thus it is among the excepted in His statement: 'Except whom God wills' [al-Naml 27:87]. What al-Subki said is the chosen view among the people of truth, and the author specifically mentioned him because of his deep knowledge in the sciences until he encompassed the rational and transmitted.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage addresses the theological dispute over whether the soul (nafs/ruh) perishes at the first trumpet blast (nafkh al-surah). The author begins by citing the poem line: 'And concerning the annihilation of the soul at the blast, there is disagreement, and al-Subki preferred its survival, as is known.' Then the commentary explains: the difference is about the passing away of the soul's form at Israfil's first blast. One group argues it perishes, citing the Qur'anic verse 'Everyone upon it will perish' (55:26). Another group holds it does not perish. Before the first blast, there is consensus that the soul remains even after the body's destruction, experiencing reward or punishment. The first blast is called the blast of annihilation; all living beings either die (if not already dead) or faint (if already dead, like the prophets). Exceptions include the four archangels, houris, and Moses, as he had already been struck unconscious in the world. All prophets regain their souls after death but then faint at the first blast except Moses. Then the second blast (blast of resurrection) occurs, where God gathers souls in the Trumpet, which has holes equal to the number of souls, and each soul goes to its body without error. Between the two blasts is forty years. Next, the author explains al-Subki's preference: he chose the view that the soul survives, based on consensus about survival after death for grave questioning, and the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity). Thus, the soul is included in the exception 'except whom God wills' (27:87). Al-Subki's position is the chosen one among Ahl al-Haqq, and the author highlights him due to his mastery of rational and transmitted sciences.

Key Takeaway

Dispute over the Annihilation of the Tailbone
The author defines 'ajb al-dhanab and mentions the dispute, with Al-Muzani affirming its perishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning and significance of 'ajb al-dhanab (the tailbone) in the context of resurrection, and the dispute over its annihilation, particularly al-Muzani's position that it perishes.

Core Idea
The tailbone is like the soul in resurrection; but al-Muzani held it perishes.

In this passage, the author defines a key term in resurrection theology: the tailbone ('ajb al-dhanab). The poem compares it to the soul, but notes a dispute with al-Muzani affirming its perishment. The commentary then explains the word's linguistic variations. This lesson will clarify what the tailbone is and why its annihilation matters.

Guided Path
1
Read the poem line and translation
Read the Arabic poem line and its literal translation. Notice that the tailbone is compared to the soul, and al-Muzani is mentioned as affirming its perishment.
The poem is a couplet from the Jawharat al-Tawhid.
2
Understand the linguistic explanation
The commentary explains that the word 'ajb has multiple valid pronunciations (six dialects). It also clarifies that 'ajb al-dhanab is a construct phrase meaning the tailbone itself.
This linguistic detail shows the precision of classical scholarship.
3
Identify the dispute
The passage highlights that al-Muzani held that the tailbone perishes, contrary to the view that it remains as the basis for resurrection. Consider why this matters for theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخلافُ في فناءِ عَجْبِ الذَّنَبِ]
عَجْبُ الذَّنَبْ كَالرُّوْحِ لَكِنْ صَحَّحَا المُزَنِيُّ لِلْبِلَى وَوَضَّحَا
قوله : (عَجْبُ الذَّنَبْ كَالرُّوْحِ) (العجب) بفتح العين وسكون الجيم وآخره باء موحدة وقد تُبدل ميماً، وبعضهم يحكي تثليث أوله فيهما، فلغاته ست. وإضافته للذَّنَب من إضافة المماثل لمماثله فقولهم : عَجب الذنب : معناه عَجْبُ الذَّنَبْ
[The dispute over the annihilation of the tailbone] The tailbone is like the soul, but al-Muzani affirmed its perishment and clarified. His saying: 'The tailbone is like the soul'—(al-'ajb) with a fatḥa on the 'ayn, a sukūn on the jīm, and ending with a single bā, and it may be replaced with a mīm; some relate that the first letter can have three vowellings for both, so it has six dialects. Its idafa to al-dhanab is an idafa of something similar to its similar, so their saying 'ajb al-dhanab' means the tailbone (ajb al-dhanab).
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage presents the dispute over the annihilation of the 'ajb al-dhanab (the tailbone or coccyx). The poem line states: 'The tailbone is like the soul, but al-Muzani affirmed its perishment and clarified.' The commentary then explains the word 'ajb linguistically: it can be pronounced with a fatḥa on the 'ayn and sukūn on the jīm, ending with a bā, sometimes replaced with a mīm; the first letter may have three possible vowellings, giving six dialects. The phrase 'ajb al-dhanab is a construct (idafa) of one similar to another, so it simply means the tailbone. The passage is cut off before completing the doctrinal discussion, but the core is that al-Muzani held that the tailbone perishes (contrary to those who say it remains as the basis for resurrection).

The Second Blast and the Soul's Persistence
Describes the second blast and argues for the soul's persistence using Subki's opinion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the second blast of the trumpet and the rational proof (istishab) for the soul's continuous existence after death.

Core Idea
The soul persists after death based on the principle of continuity (istishab) and the events of the grave.

This lesson explores two related topics from the sam‘iyyat (audibles) of the afterlife: the second trumpet blast that reunites souls with bodies, and a key theological argument for the soul's persistence (baqa’) after death. Drawing on Imam al-Subki’s reasoning, we see how a legal principle (istishab) is applied to establish a doctrine about the soul's state between death and resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Understand the second blast
Read the description of the second blast: Allah gathers souls in the trumpet, comes out to bodies without error. Note the time gap of forty years between blasts.
This is a concrete event in the afterlife.
2
Learn al-Subki's argument
Al-Subki argues for the soul's persistence using istishab: the principle that something remains as it was until evidence changes it. The evidence includes the soul's experience in the grave (questioning, bliss/punishment).
The verse 'except whom Allah wills' is an exception.
3
Recognize the scholarly endorsement
The author states that al-Subki's view is the chosen one among the people of truth, and al-Subki is mentioned due to his mastery of both rational and transmitted sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات الصور النفخة الثانية، وتُسمَّى نفخة البعث، فيجمع الله الأرواح في الصور عند النفخة الثانية، وفيه نَقْبٌ بعددها، فتخرج منه الأرواح إلى أجسادها، فلا تُخطئ روح جسدها، وبين النفختين أربعون عاماً على ما في بعض الطرق. قوله : (وَاسْتَظْهَرَ السُّبْكِي بَقَاهَا اللَّذْ عُرِف بتخفيف الياء وتسهيل ألف بقاها، وتسكين الذال لغة في (الذي) اختار الإمام تقي الدين السبكي في تفسيره المسمَّى بـ «الدر النظيم» من هذا الاختلافِ القول ببقائها الذي عهد سابقاً؛ لأنهم اتفقوا على بقائها بعد الموت لسؤالها في القبر وجوابها وتنعيمها أو تعذيبها فيه، والأصل في كل باق استمراره حتى يظهر ما يصرف عنه، فالدليل على بقائها الاستصحاب، فتكون من المستثنى بقوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا مَن شَاءَ اللهُ﴾ [النَّمل: ۸۷]، وما قاله السبكي هو المختار عند أهل الحق، وإنما خصه المصنف بالذكر لتبحُرِه في الفنون حتى أحاط بالمعقول والمنقول.
The sam‘iyyat: the second blast of the trumpet, called the blast of resurrection; Allah gathers the souls in the trumpet at the second blast, and in it there are holes according to their number, so the souls come out from it to their bodies, and no soul misses its body. Between the two blasts is forty years according to some narrations. His statement: (And al-Subki favored its persistence, which is known with the lightening of the ya’ and the simplification of the alif of baqaha, and the sukun of the dhal is a dialect in (alladhi)). Imam Taqi al-Din al-Subki chose in his commentary called al-Durr al-Nazim from this disagreement the opinion of its persistence as previously known, because they agreed upon its persistence after death due to its questioning in the grave, its answering, and its being given bliss or punishment therein. The principle regarding every abiding thing is its continuity until something appears that turns it away, so the evidence for its persistence is istishab. Thus it is among that which is excepted by His statement, exalted: 'Except whom Allah wills' [al-Naml:87]. What al-Subki said is the chosen view according to the people of truth, and the author specifically mentioned him due to his deep knowledge in the various fields until he encompassed the rational and transmitted sciences.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage first describes the second blast of the trumpet (the blast of resurrection), where Allah gathers the souls in the trumpet and then sends them to their bodies without error. It mentions that between the two blasts there are forty years according to some narrations. Then it comments on the line from the poem: 'And al-Subki favored its persistence', explaining that Imam Taqi al-Din al-Subki, in his tafsir al-Durr al-Nazim, chose the view that the soul persists after death. The reason given is that all scholars agree that the soul remains after death because it is questioned in the grave, responds, and experiences bliss or punishment. The author applies a legal principle (istishab): anything that continues to exist remains as it was until there is evidence to the contrary. Thus, the soul's persistence is based on this principle, and it is considered part of the exception in the Quranic verse 'except whom Allah wills'. The author concludes that al-Subki's view is the one chosen by the people of truth, and Ibn al-Muqri mentions al-Subki specifically because of his mastery in both rational and transmitted sciences.

Key Terms
نفخة البعث
استصحاب
سبكي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the soul ceases to exist after death until resurrection.
Correction: The passage argues that the soul persists based on istishab (continuity) and agreement on its experience in the grave (questioning, bliss/punishment).

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence al-Subki uses for the soul's persistence after death?
A) Direct Qur'anic stating the soul is immortal
B) Istishab (continuity of the previous state) and agreement on events in the grave
C) A rational proof that the soul is non-physical
D) Consensus that the soul returns to the body before resurrection

Key Takeaway
The soul persists after death based on the principle of istishab and the universally accepted events of the grave.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage affirms that your soul will persist after death and immediately face bliss or punishment. If you truly believed this will happen tonight, what would you do differently in the next hour?
?
Al-Subki used the principle of istishab—assuming continuity unless proven otherwise. Is there a harmful habit or belief you have assumed cannot change? What evidence do you have that it must continue, and what would it take to break that continuity?
?
The exception 'except whom Allah wills' reminds us that even the soul's persistence is under Allah's control. Have you ever relied on your own efforts or knowledge as if they were guaranteed? How can you live today in complete dependence on Allah's will rather than your own plans?

The Tailbone: Between Annihilation and Eternal Preservation
Defines the tailbone and presents the two views on its annihilation, with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two opposing views on whether the tailbone perishes or remains eternally, and the evidence cited for each.

Core Idea
The tailbone is a unique bone that the earth never consumes, serving as the basis for resurrection.

This passage introduces a fascinating point of theological and eschatological discussion: the fate of the tailbone (ʿajb al-dhanab). Is it subject to decay like the rest of the body, or does it persist miraculously as the starting point for resurrection? This lesson will clarify the definitions, the positions of key scholars, and the scriptural proofs they employed.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic source and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the detailed linguistic analysis at the start.
2
Focus on the definition of the tailbone
Identify what the tailbone is anatomically and linguistically. Note it is compared to the soul and why.
The comparison to the soul sets up the two views.
3
Understand the two views
Identify al-Muzani's view (annihilation) and the stronger view (persistence). Note the evidence each uses.
Al-Muzani uses the Quran; the hadith support persistence.
4
Analyze the evidence for each view
Compare the Quranic verse 'Everything is perishing' with the hadith that the tailbone does not decay. Why does the author favor the hadith?
Consider the principle that specific evidence can qualify general evidence.
5
Consider the debate on the cause of its persistence
Examine the discussion on whether persistence is devotional or based on a cause. Understand why the devotional view is preferred.
The proposed cause (a sign for angels) is deemed weak.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخلافُ في فناءِ عَجْبِ الذَّنَبِ عَجْبُ الذَّنَبْ كَالرُّوْحِ لَكِنْ صَحَّحَا المُزَنِيُّ لِلْبِلَى وَوَضَّحَا قوله : (عَجْبُ الذَّنَبْ كَالرُّوْحِ) (العجب) بفتح العين وسكون الجيم وآخره باء موحدة وقد تُبدل ميماً، وبعضهم يحكي تثليث أوله فيهما، فلغاته ست. وإضافته للذَّنَب من إضافة المماثل لمماثله فقولهم : عَجب الذنب : معناه عَجْبُ شبيه بالذنب، وهو عظم كالخردلة في آخر سلسلة الظهر في العُصْعُص مختص بالإنسان كمغرز الذنب للدابة، وهو بكسر الراء من باب (ضرب)، وتشبيهه بالروح في جريان الاختلاف في الفناء على قولين والمشهور منهما أنه لا يفنى لكن لا بقيد وقت النفخ، وإن كان الخلاف في المشبه به مُقيداً به، كما صرح به المصنف في قوله : (وفي فنا النفس لدى النفخ اختلف). قوله: (لَكِنْ صَحْحًا المُزَنِيُّ لِلْبِلَى) أي: لكن صحح الإمام إسماعيل بن يحيى المزني، وهو منسوبٌ لـ (مُزَينة) اسم قبيلة القول بأنَّ عَجب الذنب يبلى ويفني، تمسكاً بظاهر قوله تعالى : كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍ ﴾ [الرَّحمن (٢٦] ، وفناء الكل يستلزم فناء الجزء. وقوله : (وَوَضَحَا) أي : بين صحة ما ذهب إليه ووافقه ابن قتيبة، وقال: إنه آخر ما يبلى من الميت والأقوى في النظر أنه لا يبلى لحديث الصحيحين: «ليس من الإنسان شيء إلا يبلى إلا عظماً واحداً؛ وهو عجب الذنب، منه خُلِقَ الخلقُ يوم القيامة»، ولحديث مسلم : «كلُّ ابن آدم يأكله التراب إلا عجب الذنب منه خُلِق، ومنه يُرَكَّبُ»، وفي حديثه الآخر: «إن في الإنسان عظماً لا تأكله الأرض أبداً»، واختلف هل بقاؤه تعبدي أو مُعلَّل، والأرجح أنه تعبدي لضعف ما علل به القائل بأنه معلل، فإنه علله بجواز كونه جعل علامة للملائكة الموكلين بالإعادة على إحياء كل إنسان بجواهره التي كانت في الدنيا، ووجه ضعفه أن الملائكة لا يخفى عليهم هذا الأمر، مع أنهم يعيدون كلَّ إنسان بجواهره بأمر الله على أنه يجوز اللَّبْسُ فيه نفسه
The disagreement over the annihilation of the tailbone. The tailbone is like the soul, but al-Muzani corrected (the view) of decay and clarified it. His statement: (The tailbone is like the soul). (al-‘Ajb) with a fatha on the ‘ayn and sukun on the jim, ending with a ba’ with one dot, and it may be replaced with a mim; some relate the triplication of its first letter in both, so it has six dialects. Its addition to al-dhanab is an addition of a similar to its similar, so they say: ‘ajb al-dhanab – its meaning is a ‘ajb similar to the tail, and it is a bone like a mustard seed at the end of the spinal column in the coccyx, specific to humans, like the insertion of the tail of an animal; it (the word) is with a kasra on the ra’ from the pattern of daraba. Its being likened to the soul is due to the flow of disagreement over annihilation on two views, the more famous of which is that it does not perish, but not restricted to the time of the blast, even if the disagreement regarding that which is likened (the soul) is restricted to it, as the author clarified in his statement: 'And regarding the annihilation of the soul at the blast, there is disagreement.' His statement: (but al-Muzani corrected for decay) means: but Imam Isma‘il ibn Yahya al-Muzani – attributed to (Muzayna) the name of a tribe – corrected the view that the tailbone decays and perishes, adhering to the apparent meaning of His statement, exalted: 'Everyone upon it is perishing' [al-Rahman:26], and the annihilation of the whole necessitates the annihilation of the part. And his statement: (and clarified) means: he made clear the correctness of what he went to, and Ibn Qutayba agreed with him, and he said: It is the last thing that decays from the deceased. But the stronger view in consideration is that it does not decay due to the hadith of the two Sahihs: 'There is nothing of a person that does not decay except one bone, and it is the tailbone; from it the creation is created on the Day of Resurrection.' And due to the hadith of Muslim: 'Every son of Adam is consumed by the earth except the tailbone; from it he was created, and from it he will be reconstituted.' And in his other hadith: 'Verily, in a person there is a bone that the earth never consumes.' And they disagreed whether its persistence is devotional (ta‘abbudi) or based on a cause (mu‘allal); the more likely is that it is devotional due to the weakness of what was used as cause by those who claim it is based on a cause. For they gave as cause that it might be made a sign for the angels charged with resurrection to revive each person with his substances that were in the world. The weakness of this is that the angels are not unaware of this matter, especially since they resurrect each person with his substances by the command of Allah, and it is possible that there is confusion in this matter itself.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage begins a new subject: the disagreement over the annihilation of the tailbone (ʿajb al-dhanab). It first quotes a line from the poem: 'The tailbone is like the soul, but al-Muzani corrected the view of decay and clarified it.' Then it provides a detailed definition and linguistic analysis of the word 'ajb, noting its various pronunciations. It explains that the tailbone is a small bone at the end of the spine, like a mustard seed, specific to humans, analogous to the insertion of an animal's tail. The likening of the tailbone to the soul refers to the fact that there are two views regarding its annihilation, just as there are two views regarding the soul's annihilation at the time of the blast. The more famous view is that the tailbone does not perish, but this view is not restricted to the time of the blast, unlike the disagreement about the soul. It then explains al-Muzani's position: he held that the tailbone decays and perishes, based on the apparent meaning of the verse 'Everyone upon it is perishing' [al-Rahman:26], arguing that the annihilation of the whole (all creatures) implies the annihilation of the part (the tailbone). Al-Muzani was supported by Ibn Qutayba, who said it is the last part to decay. However, the author deems the stronger view to be that it does not decay, citing three hadiths from Bukhari and Muslim: (1) Nothing decays except one bone, the tailbone, from which creation is recreated; (2) Every part is consumed except the tailbone, from which it was created and reconstituted; (3) There is a bone that the earth never consumes. Then the author discusses whether its persistence is devotional (taʿabbudi, based purely on divine command) or based on a cause (muʿallal, with a rational explanation). He concludes that devotional is more likely because the proposed cause – that it serves as a sign for the angels to identify each person's substances – is weak: angels are not ignorant of this matter, and they revive each person by God's command, and confusion is still possible.

Correction: Authentic hadith clearly state that the tailbone is the one bone that does not decay and is the basis for resurrection.

Key Takeaway
The tailbone is a miraculous bone that does not decay, serving as the origin for bodily resurrection, with strong evidence from authentic hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The tailbone is a tiny, unseen bone that Allah preserves as the seed of your return. What unseen acts of obedience or disobedience have you stored up that will be resurrected with you? Are you ready for that moment when every atom of your existence is reassembled to face your Lord?
?
You claim to believe in the resurrection, but do your daily choices reflect that conviction? If you knew that your tailbone was the proof that your body will be rebuilt, would you treat your body as a trust to be returned to Allah intact, or as a vessel for your own desires?

Specifying the General Verse 'Everything Perishes'
Explanation of specifying the general verse to exclude the soul and tailbone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the apparent generality of the Quranic verse 'Everything perishes' is specified to allow for the persistence of the soul and tailbone.

Core Idea
General Quranic verses can be specified by other texts; they are not absolute.

This lesson addresses a common question: if everything perishes except Allah, how can the soul and tailbone persist? The author of the Jawharah points out that scholars have specified the general meaning of such verses through other scriptural evidence. Let's see how this is done.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice that the author begins by quoting a line from the poem.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the objection and resolution
The objection comes from the verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face'. The resolution is that scholars have specified (takhsis) the generality of that verse.
The phrase 'قد خصصوا عمومه' is key.
3
Understand the principle of specification
In Islamic theology, general statements in revelation can be narrowed by other revealed texts. This allows for exceptions like the soul and tailbone.
This is a standard principle of usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكٌ قَدْ خَصَّصُوا عُمُوْمَهُ فَاطْلُبْ لِمَا قَدْ لَخَصُوا قوله : (وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكُ قَدْ خَصَّصُوا عُمُوْمَهُ) لما كان القول ببقاء الروح وعجب الذنب هو الراجح، أشار المصنف إلى الجواب عما يرد عليه كقوله تعالى : كُلُّ شَىءٍ هَا لِك إِلَّا وَجْهَهُ ﴾ [القصص : ۸۸] ؛ إذ مقتضاه أن كل ما سواه تعالى محكوم عليه بالهلاك.
And everything is perishing; they have specified its generality, so seek what they have summarized. His statement: (And everything is perishing; they have specified its generality). Since the view of the persistence of the soul and the tailbone is the stronger one, the author indicated the answer to what might be objected against it, like His statement, exalted: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' [al-Qasas:88]; for its apparent meaning is that everything other than Him, exalted, is subject to perishing.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection: if the soul and tailbone persist, how do we understand the Quranic verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' [al-Qasas:88], which seems to say that all creatures perish? The author quotes a line from the poem: 'And everything is perishing; they have specified its generality, so seek what they have summarized.' This means that scholars have specified the general meaning of such verses by other texts that indicate some things do not perish. Since the stronger view is that the soul and tailbone persist, these items are exceptions to the general rule of perishing. The author indicates that this is the answer to the objection: the generality of the verse is not absolute; it is specified by the evidence for the persistence of the soul and tailbone.

Key Terms
عموم
تخصيص
هلاك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Everything perishes' must be interpreted literally and absolutely, so nothing can persist.
Correction: General Qur'anic verses can be specified by other revealed texts; the persistence of the soul and tailbone is supported by evidence.

Checkpoint
How does the author resolve the conflict between the persistence of the soul/tailbone and the verse 'Everything perishes'?
A) The verse is abrogated
B) The verse's generality is specified by other texts
C) The soul and tailbone are not part of 'everything'
D) The verse applies only to the afterlife

Key Takeaway
The generality of a Quranic verse can be specified by other scriptural evidence, allowing for exceptions such as the persistence of the soul and tailbone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The scholars specified the general verse based on other evidence. Do you trust that the Quran and Sunnah together give a complete picture, even when a single verse seems to contradict a belief? How does this affect your approach to understanding difficult texts?

The Survival of the Coccyx Bone
Definition of 'ajb al-dhanab and discussion of its survival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological debate about the survival of the coccyx bone (عجب الذنب), the evidence from hadith, and the distinction between devotional and rational explanations.

Core Idea
The coccyx bone's survival is a revealed truth, not a rational deduction.

This lesson examines a specific eschatological detail: the fate of a small bone at the base of the spine called 'ajb al-dhanab. While some scholars argued it decays based on a general Quranic verse, authentic hadith assert it remains intact as the seed of resurrection. The author also explains why this survival is best understood as a devotional truth beyond human reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition and initial disagreement
Read the definition of 'ajb al-dhanab and note the two opinions on its annihilation: the famous view that it does not perish, and al-Muzani's view that it does.
The bone is compared to the soul in terms of disagreement.
2
Examine the hadith evidence for survival
Study the hadith from al-Bukhari and Muslim that explicitly state the coccyx does not decay and is the basis for resurrection. This evidence outweighs the general Quranic verse.
The hadith are considered stronger by the author.
3
Analyze the debate: devotional vs. rational
Understand why the author favors the devotional (ta'abbudi) view over the rational (mu'allal) view, noting the weakness of the rational argument about angels.
This shows the priority of revelation over human reasoning in such matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبيه بالذنب، وهو عظم كالخردلة في آخر سلسلة الظهر في العُصْعُص مختص بالإنسان كمغرز الذنب للدابة، وهو بكسر الراء من باب (ضرب)، وتشبيهه بالروح في جريان الاختلاف في الفناء على قولين والمشهور منهما أنه لا يفنى لكن لا بقيد وقت النفخ، وإن كان الخلاف في المشبه به مُقيداً به، كما صرح به المصنف في قوله : (وفي فنا النفس لدى النفخ اختلف).
قوله: (لَكِنْ صَحْحًا المُزَنِيُّ لِلْبِلَى) أي: لكن صحح الإمام إسماعيل بن يحيى المزني، وهو منسوبٌ لـ (مُزَينة) اسم قبيلة القول بأنَّ عَجب الذنب يبلى ويفني، تمسكاً بظاهر قوله تعالى : كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍ ﴾ [الرَّحمن (٢٦] ، وفناء الكل يستلزم فناء الجزء.
وقوله : (وَوَضَحَا) أي : بين صحة ما ذهب إليه ووافقه ابن قتيبة، وقال: إنه آخر ما يبلى من الميت والأقوى في النظر أنه لا يبلى لحديث الصحيحين»: ليس من الإنسان شيء إلا يبلى إلا عظماً واحداً؛ وهو عجب الذنب، منه خُلِقَ الخلقُ يوم القيامة» (۱) ، ولحديث مسلم : كلُّ ابن آدم يأكله التراب إلا عجب الذنب منه خُلِق، ومنه يُرَكَّبُ (۲) ، وفي حديثه الآخر: إن في الإنسان عظماً لا تأكله الأرض أبداً (۳) ، واختلف هل بقاؤه تعبدي أو مُعلَّل، والأرجح أنه تعبدي لضعف ما علل به القائل بأنه معلل، فإنه علله بجواز كونه جعل علامة للملائكة الموكلين بالإعادة على إحياء كل إنسان بجواهره التي كانت في الدنيا، ووجه ضعفه أن الملائكة لا يخفى عليهم هذا الأمر، مع أنهم يعيدون كلَّ إنسان بجواهره بأمر الله على أنه يجوز اللَّبْسُ فيه نفسه
Similar to the tail, and it is a bone like a mustard seed at the end of the spinal column in the coccyx, specific to humans, like the insertion of the tail for an animal. It is with a kasrah on the ra' from the pattern (daraba). Its comparison to the soul [applies] regarding the occurrence of disagreement about annihilation (fana') on two opinions, the more well-known of which is that it does not perish, but not restricted to the time of the Blast, even though the disagreement concerning the thing compared is restricted to it, as the author stated in his words: 'And regarding the annihilation of the soul at the time of the Blast, they differed.' His words: 'But al-Muzani declared correct [the view of] decay' meaning: But Imam Isma'il ibn Yahya al-Muzani, who is attributed to (Muzayna) the name of a tribe, declared correct the opinion that the coccyx decays and perishes, adhering to the apparent meaning of His statement, Exalted: 'Everyone upon it is perishing' [ar-Rahman 26], and the annihilation of the whole necessitates the annihilation of the part. And his words: 'And he clarified' meaning: he made clear the correctness of what he went to, and Ibn Qutaybah agreed with him, and said: It is the last thing that decays from the dead. But the stronger [view] in consideration is that it does not decay, due to the hadith of the Two Sahihs: 'There is nothing of the human that does not decay except one bone, which is the coccyx; from it creation was created on the Day of Resurrection,' and due to the hadith of Muslim: 'Every son of Adam is eaten by the earth except the coccyx; from it he was created, and from it he will be recomposed,' and in his other hadith: 'There is in the human a bone that the earth will never eat.' And they differed whether its survival is devotional (ta'abbudi) or rational (mu'allal). The preferable view is that it is devotional due to the weakness of what the one who said it is rational argued with, for he argued by the possibility that it was made a sign for the angels entrusted with resurrection to revive every human with his atoms that were in the world. The weakness of this is that the angels are not unaware of this matter, especially since they revive every human with his atoms by the command of God, and it is possible for confusion to occur regarding it itself.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage defines 'ajb al-dhanab (the coccyx bone) and discusses the theological debate over its annihilation (fana') and survival (baqa'). The author begins by defining 'ajb al-dhanab as a small bone at the base of the spine, unique to humans, and compares its status to the soul: both are subjects of disagreement regarding whether they perish. The more famous view is that the coccyx does not perish, but this survival is not tied to a specific time like the Blast of the Trumpet. Next, the author explains al-Muzani's view that the coccyx does decay, based on the Quranic verse 'Everyone upon it is perishing' (55:26), arguing that the whole includes the part. However, the author clarifies that the stronger position, supported by authentic hadith from al-Bukhari and Muslim, is that the coccyx does not decay. The hadith explicitly state that this bone will not be eaten by the earth and will be the basis for resurrection. The author then notes a further disagreement: whether the survival of the coccyx is a devotional matter (ta'abbudi, accepted without rational explanation) or rationally explicable (mu'allal). The preferred view is that it is devotional, because the rational argument (that it serves as a marker for angels) is weak: angels do not need such a marker, as they already know everything by God's command.

Key Terms
عجب الذنب
الفناء
التعبدي
المعلل
الصحيحان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Correction: The survival of the coccyx is a theological matter based on hadith (revealed texts), with rational arguments considered weak. It is accepted as a devotional truth, not a scientific fact.
